<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="iv-fluorescence-microscope">IV. FLUORESCENCE MICROSCOPE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-fluorescence-microscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Certain chemical compounds absorb light and reemit part of the radiant energy as light of longer wavelength. Such substances are called fluorescent and the phenomenon is termed as fluorescence. In fluorescence microscopy, a high intensity mercury lamp is used as the light source, which emits white light. The exciter filter transmits only blue light to the specimen and blocks out all the colors. The blue light is reflected downward to the specimen by the dichroic mirror. The specimen is stained with fluorescent dye (acrydine orange). Only certain portions of the specimen retain the dye, others do not. The stained portion of the specimen absorb blue light and emit green light, which passes upwards, penetrate the dichroic mirror and reaches the barrier filter. This filter allows only green light to pass through and the eye receives only green light emitted from the specimen against the black background whereas unstained portions are invisible. Also, ultraviolet light is used to excite molecules so that they release light of a different wavelength.</p>
<p>This technique is especially important in <strong>immunology</strong> in which the reactions of antigens and antibodies are studied in great detail. Fluorescent antibody staining is now widely used in diagnostic procedures to determine whether an antigen is present. Not all bacteria get stained with fluorescent chemicals. <strong>Excitation and fluorescence with chromatic beam splitters.</strong> Similar to the interference filters these are specially coated mirrors used under <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>45</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">45^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to the illuminating beam. They reflect certain spectral ranges, while others are completely transmitted. The separating line between reflection and transmission may be set at any point of the spectrum. 1. Exciting radiation, 2. Fluorescence emission</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b9e79fdb.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg">
Figure 17: Working Principles of Fluorescence Microscope</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-electron-microscope">B) Electron Microscope<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-electron-microscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In electron microscope, short beam of electrons and magnetic condenser lenses are employed to produce the image. The electrons have short wavelength, which helps in better resolution. It is possible to resolve objects as small as 10° A, which is 100 times more than that of light microscope. It can magnify object up to 200,000X.</p>
<p>In electron microscope, a hot tungsten filament forms the source of electrons. The object is placed in the path of moving electrons. Since electrons move only in the vacuum, the entire path of electrons should be kept under vacuum. The magnetic condenser lens causes the primary magnification. A second magnetic lens amplifies the primary image and this image is viewed on a fluorescent screen or captured on photographic plates. There are two types of electron microscope.</p>
<p>a. Transmission electron microscope (TEM)
b. Scanning electron microscope (SEM)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-transmission-electron-microscope">a) TRANSMISSION ELECTRON MICROSCOPE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-transmission-electron-microscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A high voltage established between the filament and the anode accelerates the electrons from the hot tungsten filament. The electron beam is focused on the specimen with an electromagnetic condenser. Ultra thin sections of the specimen must be prepared since electrons can penetrate matter only a short distance. This is done by embedding or freezing the specimen and sectioning it with a diamond or a glass Knife. The sections are floated in water and collected in a copper grid. They are stained with heavy metals such as gold or palladium and kept within the evacuated column of the electron microscope.</p>
<p>TEM has a projector lens that project the image onto a fluorescent viewing screen or film plate, because the beam cannot be viewed directly. With TEM greater resolution and higher magnifications than light and Scanning Electron Microscope can be obtained. In TEM, the differential scattering of electrons by the specimen makes the contrast. Since most of the atoms of the biological material are of low mass, the contrast of the specimen is low. Staining with heavy metals such as platinum, uranium or tungsten can increase the contrast.</p>
<p>They are of various types such as,</p>
<p>a. Positive staining: The heavy metals are fixed on the specimen.
b. Negative staining: It is used to increase the electron opacity of the surrounding area.</p>
<p>Two techniques commonly employed for the observation of biological specimen are:</p>
<p>a. Metal shadowing: The dried specimen is exposed at an acute angle to a stream of heavy metals like platinum, palladium or gold and thereby producing an image, that reveals the three-dimensional structure of the object.
b. Freeze fracturing: The frozen specimen is fractured with a knife, and the exposed surface is coated with a heavy metal (Gold) at an acute angle. A</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO

71</p>
<p>supporting layer of carbon is evaporated on the metal surface. Then the specimen is destroyed and the replica is examined. This method is used for studying cell wall and cell membrane. The penetrating power of electrons is low; hence the ultra thin sections of the specimens should be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-scanning-electron-microscope">b) SCANNING ELECTRON MICROSCOPE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-scanning-electron-microscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The specimen is coated with a thin layer of heavy metal and the specimen is subjected to a narrow beam of electrons, which rapidly moves and scans the surface of the specimen. The irradiated specimen depending upon its physical and chemical composition will release secondary electrons. These secondary electrons are then collected by anode detector, which generates an electronic signal. Then the electronic signal is scanned in TV system to produce an image on a cathode ray tube. Magnification on SEM is about 75,000 to 1,00,000 times.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="limitations">Limitations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limitations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Specimen is kept under high vacuum on the path of electron beam. So, living cells can't be examined.
b. Electrons have low penetration capacity, hence ultra thin section and staining should be done which is time consuming and also sometimes alter or distort the structures of microorganisms.
c. High cost and specialized techniques prevent its use in all microbiology labs in spite of greater magnification and resolution.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-of-microscope">Care Of Microscope<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-microscope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevent-damage-to-the-40x-objectives">Prevent damage to the 40x objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevent-damage-to-the-40x-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Immediately remove any immersion oil that accidentally comes into contact with the 40x objective. Because the 40x lens is located next to the 100x lens and because it is also a long lens, it is easy for it to come into contact with immersion oil accidentally. The 40x objective is not sealed against oil penetration, and any immersion oil left in contact with this objective will penetrate the lens and be deposited on the inside of the lower lens. Only the manufacturer can repair, after dismantling the objective lens.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevent-damage-to-the-100x-objective">Prevent damage to the 100x objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevent-damage-to-the-100x-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lower the stage before removing a slide.</li>
<li>After finishing a microscopic examination, immediately clean the immersion oil from the objective with lens paper and commercially prepared lens cleaner. If this is not done, the oil may thicken and harden over time and affect the optical performance of the lens.</li>
<li>To protect the 100x objective lens, the objective should be rotated up when the microscope is not in use.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="storage">Storage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#storage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In warm humid climates, fungal growth is easily established on lenses and prisms. The microscope must be stored in dry conditions when not in use to prevent fungal growth on glass surfaces. For example, the microscope could be kept in a “warm cupboard” with a constant temperature and low humidity. Lenses and prism heads could be stored in airtight boxes containing desiccant (not containing cobalt chloride).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-procedures">Cleaning procedures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-procedures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cleaning of the microscope is one of the most important routines and must be considered essential. The following materials are required:</p>
<ol>
<li>A piece of clean cloth with a similar texture to that of a handkerchief.</li>
<li>A bottle of lens cleaning solution which can be obtained from opticians. Normally, it does not affect the lenses’ protective coating nor the adhesives or cements used in their assembly. Among widely used cleaning liquids are ethyl ether, xylene and white gasoline.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Warning</strong>: Some manufacturers do not recommend using alcohol or acetone as these can affect (dissolve) the cements and adhesives used for attaching lenses.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Lens paper. This can normally be obtained from opticians. If it is not possible to obtain this material, it can be substituted with soft absorbent paper or with medicinal type cotton. Also a piece of soft silk can be used.</li>
<li>A piece of very fine chamois. This can be obtained from shoe shops.</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
73</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>A rubber (nasal) bulb for blowing air. A device can be made in the laboratory by connecting a Pasteur pipette to the rubber bulb.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A plastic cover to protect the microscope from its external environment when not in use. A cloth bag with a texture similar to handkerchief material can also be used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A soft camel hair brush or a fine paint brush. Importantly, the brush's hair should be natural, of uniform length with a very soft texture, dry and free from grease. It is possible to obtain this in photography stores. Also, it is possible to find an equivalent in shops supplying cosmetics.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A 250 g packet of desiccant (silica gel). This is used to control the humidity in the microscope's storage box if it is airtight. It changes colour when it is saturated by humidity to detect when it needs to be substituted or renewed. When it is in good condition, the colour is generally blue; when it is saturated with humidity, it is pink.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bulbs and replacement fuses. These should be of the same model as those installed by the manufacturer or of equivalent characteristics.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: All required materials for cleaning must be kept clean and stored in containers that protect them from their external environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-of-the-optical-elements">Cleaning of the optical elements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-of-the-optical-elements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In a microscope, there are two types of optical elements: those external in contact with their outside environment and those internal, inside the body of the microscope and more protected (objectives, eyepieces, mirrors, prisms, condenser, illuminator, etc.). The cleaning procedures, although similar, differ with regard to the care and precautions.</p>
<p>The external optical elements of eyepieces, objectives, condenser and illuminator are cleaned by gently brushing their surfaces with the camel hair brush. This removes dust particles. The rubber bulb is then used to blow streams of air onto the lenses' surface to ensure that these are free from dust. If dust is found adhered to the optical surface, a piece of very soft clean cloth is used with small circular movements, without exercising too much pressure on the lens. The nasal bulb is used again to blow air on the lens to remove adhered particles. A piece of fine chamois can also be used. If so, place the chamois at the end of a small cylindrical object with a slightly smaller diameter than that of the lens. Without exercising much pressure, rotate gently on the lens surface. Finally, air is blown onto the lens surface with the nasal aspirator. This is sufficient to clean the external surfaces. The piece of chamois can be humidified with distilled water if necessary.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Under adequate conditions of installation, interior surfaces of optical elements should not be affected by dust or particles. If for some reason, particles are detected, it is necessary to open them to carry out the cleaning process. An eyepiece or objective must never be opened if there is not a clean environment to carry out the cleaning procedure. Clean with a camel hair brush and with the nasal aspirator according to the procedure explained previously. It is not recommended to dismount the objectives for any reason as this could alter the tolerances achieved by the manufacturer. If dismounted, it would be necessary to realign the elements and this is only</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
74</p>
<p>feasible if the manufacturer's precise instructions are followed. Cleaning of the objectives will be limited to keeping the front and back lenses clean.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>If immersion oil residues are detected on the lens surface, remove using lens paper or medicinal type cotton. The lens' surface must be then cleaned with a solution composed of 80% ether petroleum and 20% 2-Propanol.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-of-the-microscope-s-body">Cleaning of the microscope's body<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-of-the-microscope-s-body" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The microscope's body can be cleaned with a detergent solution to remove external filth and cut the grease and oil. This must be applied with a small brush. After the grease and filth have been removed, the microscope's body must be cleaned with a 50/50 solution of distilled water and 95% ethanol.</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: This solution is not adequate for cleaning optical surfaces.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>The parts integrated in adjustment mechanisms for the macro/micrometric (thick and fine) adjustment, the condenser and the stage or platform must be lubricated periodically with refined machine oil to facilitate smooth movement.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance">Maintenance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="microscope-maintenance">Microscope maintenance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microscope-maintenance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Among the most important steps for maintaining a microscope in suitable operation conditions are the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Verify the adjustment of the mechanical stage. It must move gently in all directions (X-Y) and must stay in the position selected by the microscopist.</li>
<li>Test the focus adjustment mechanism. The focus selected by the microscopist must remain stable. The height must not change from that assigned by the microscopist.</li>
<li>Verify the functioning of the diaphragm.</li>
<li>Clean all the mechanical components.</li>
<li>Lubricate the microscope according to the manufacturer's recommendations.</li>
<li>Confirm the adjustment of the specimen holder (gripping device).</li>
<li>Verify the optical alignment.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="precautions">Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Avoid cleaning optical components with ethanol because it affects the optical elements. Also, do not clean the base of the platform with xylene or acetone.</li>
<li>Do not use ordinary paper to clean lenses as it could scratch their surface.</li>
<li>To prevent leaving fingerprints, do not touch lenses with bare fingers.</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
75</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>
<p>Do not clean the eyepieces' lenses or objectives with cloth or paper, because the coating covering the optical elements could deteriorate. Clean these surfaces with a camel hair brush or by blowing air with a nasal aspirator.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid leaving the microscope without the eyepieces. Place stoppers on these to prevent dust and particles from entering the binocular head.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not leave the microscope stored inside a box in humid environments.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid pressing the objective against slides as it could damage the thin lamina or its front lens. Adjust the focus slowly and carefully.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keep the platform or mechanical stage clean.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not disassemble optical components since this can produce misalignments. Optical surfaces must be cleaned first with a camel hair brush and then with a chamois or lens paper.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use both hands for lifting the microscope, one hand supporting the microscope arm and the other supporting its base.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid touching the surface of the bulb with fingers when changing it. Fingerprints decrease the light intensity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verify that the feed voltage is correct in order to prolong the life span of the bulb. Whenever possible, use the lowest light intensity needed for carrying out observations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Connect the microscope to a voltage stabilizer if the feed voltage is not stable.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="special-care-in-warm-climates">Special care in warm climates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#special-care-in-warm-climates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In warm climates as well as in dry ones, the main problem affecting the microscope is dust since it affects the mechanical and the optical systems. This problem can be controlled by the following steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Always protect the microscope with a plastic cover when not in use.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After use, clean the microscope by blowing air using a nasal aspirator.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clean the lenses with a camel hair brush or with an air brush. If the dust stays adhered to optical surfaces, try to remove it with lens paper. However, rub the surface very gently to avoid scratches.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="special-antifungal-care-in-humid-climates">Special antifungal care in humid climates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#special-antifungal-care-in-humid-climates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In humid and generally warm climates, microscopes can be affected by fungi growing mainly on the surface of lenses, in the grooves of screws and under the protective paint. If the equipment is not adequately protected, it could become useless in a short period of time. The following care instructions will assist in preventing the formation of fungus.</p>
<ol>
<li>At night, store the microscope in a box equipped with an electric light of no more than 40 W. The bulb must be installed in the upper part of the box, near the binocular head and must be kept</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
76</p>
<p>on during the night. The box must have some openings to allow the air to circulate. The temperature inside the box must not exceed 50 °C so that properties of the microscope’s lubricants are not affected.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>If it is not possible to use a box with electric light, as an alternative, a drying agent such as silicone gel or rice can be used. When a drying agent is used, verify that the microscope is kept in a protected box or under a cover made of fabric similar to that of a handkerchief. Verify that the drying agent is in good condition. If this is not the case, substitute it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clean the microscope periodically. Use latex gloves if lenses must be touched. This will prevent leaving any fingerprint and decrease the risks of fungal growth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If none of the mentioned alternatives is feasible, put the microscope in a place with good air circulation. When the microscope is not in use, it may be located under direct solar light, for short periods. This reduces the humidity and the risk of fungi growing on the surfaces of the equipment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Air conditioning (temperature and humidity control) significantly prevents fungal growth on microscopes. However, this is not an option for a great number of laboratories. If the air conditioning service is not continuous in the area where the microscope is installed, precautions must be taken to control the humidity.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="removal-of-fungal-hair">Removal of fungal hair<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removal-of-fungal-hair" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Check and clean the microscope frequently using the procedures mentioned in this chapter. Control the humidity conditions where the microscope is stored. If adequate ventilation is maintained, it decreases the possibility of fungal growth on the microscope.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If fungal growth is detected, use a small piece of cotton dampened in an antifungal solution, normally ether or xylol (xylene). Rub gently making circular motions on the entire surface of the lens. An oscillatory movement can also be used, towards the front and back or left right-left, exercising a very moderate pressure on the surface of the lens. If necessary, repeat the procedure with a new piece of cotton.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When removal of the fungal hair is completed, clean with a small piece of clean cotton.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="microscope-care">Microscope care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microscope-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="daily-maintenance-after-use">Daily maintenance (after use)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily-maintenance-after-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Inspect the microscope for damage or malfunction.</li>
<li>Record any damage or malfunction in the daily microscopy maintenance sheet. Clean the parts of the microscope with a clean cloth.</li>
<li>Clean the objectives after each day’s work.</li>
<li>Ensure that immersion oil residues are removed. Do not clean any part of the microscope with</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
77</p>
<p>xylene, which will damage the microscope and is toxic.</p>
<ul>
<li>Clean the objective lens with lens cleaning tissue only. Never clean lenses with alcohol, ordinary tissues, cleaning paper, toilet paper, cotton wool or hand towels, which will scratch the lens surface.</li>
<li>Cover the microscope with a dust cover when not in use. Cover the microscope with a protective cover (of plastic or cloth). Ensure that it is kept in a well-ventilated place where the humidity and temperature are controlled. If it has a ventilated storage box equipped with a light bulb for humidity control, place the microscope inside, turn on the light and close the box.</li>
<li>Turn off the power at the end of the day, and unplug the microscope to protect it from a power surge.</li>
<li>Place the light intensity control rheostat in the lowest position and then turn off the lighting system completely.</li>
<li>Do not leave lens ports uncovered; use the port cover or sealing tape.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="frequency-each-month">Frequency: Each month<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-each-month" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Remove dust particles from the microscope’s body. Use a piece of cloth dampened with distilled water.</li>
<li>Remove dust particles from the eyepieces, objectives and condenser. Use a rubber bulb for blowing air. Next, clean the lenses’ surface with lens cleaning solution. Do not apply this solution to lenses directly, but on lens paper and then rub their surfaces gently with the wet paper.</li>
<li>Remove the slide holder mechanism, clean carefully and reinstall.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="frequency-every-six-months">Frequency: Every six months<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-every-six-months" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As a complement to the monthly maintenance routines, the following are recommended:</p>
<ol>
<li>Carry out a general visual inspection of the microscope. Verify that each component is in good condition, clean and mechanically well adjusted.</li>
<li>Verify that good ventilation conditions, temperature and humidity control are maintained in the place of installation.</li>
<li>Test the quality of the electric system that feeds the microscope. Verify the integrity of the connectors, fuses and of the incandescent light.</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
78</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="repairs">Repairs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#repairs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Site staff can replace a broken bulb or replace a blown fuse by strictly following the manufacturer's instructions. Other repairs must be performed by a qualified service engineer or technician.</li>
<li>Do not exchange lenses and ports with those of other microscopes.</li>
<li>Routine servicing, such as realignment of optics, replacement of lens and maintenance and lubrication of the stage, should be performed by a qualified service technician.</li>
<li>Record all repairs on the microscope maintenance sheet.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="changing-the-lamp-or-a-fuse">Changing the lamp or a fuse:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#changing-the-lamp-or-a-fuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Switch off the microscope and remove the plug from the mains socket. Follow the manufacturer's instructions for replacing the fuse or the lamp.</p>
<p><strong>Note.</strong> For halogen lamp use the lamp of the correct voltage and wattage. Hold the glass part of the between a piece of tissues or cloth. Finger markings on the glass will reduce the life span of the lamp. Always turn the lamp brightness control to its lowest setting before switching it on the microscope. This will help to prolong the life of the lamp.</p>
<p><strong>Fuse:</strong> Use fuse of the correct rating. If the reason for the fuse blowing is not known check for electrical fault(s).</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="laboratory-incubators">LABORATORY INCUBATORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laboratory-incubators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In microbiology, is an insulated and enclosed device that provides an optimal condition of temperature, humidity, and other environmental conditions required for the growth of organisms. An incubator is a piece of vital laboratory equipment necessary for the cultivation of microorganisms under artificial conditions.</p>
<p>An incubator can be used for the cultivation of both unicellular and multicellular organisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-parts-of-incubator">Components/Parts of Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-parts-of-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-5c5a6467.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cabinet">Cabinet<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cabinet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The cabinet is the main body of the incubator consisting of a double-walled cuboidal enclosure with a capacity ranging from 20 to 800L.</li>
<li>The outer wall is made up of stainless-steel sheets while the inner wall is made up of aluminum.</li>
<li>The space between the two walls is filled with glass wool to provide insulation to the incubator.</li>
<li>The insulation prevents heat loss and reduces electric consumption, thereby ensuring the smooth working of the device.</li>
<li>The inner wall of the incubator is provided with inward projections that support the shelves present inside the incubator.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="door">Door<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#door" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A door is present in all incubators to close the insulated cabinet.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
83</p>
<ul>
<li>The door also has insulation of its own. It is also provided with a glass that enables the visualization of the interior of the incubator during incubation without disturbing the interior environment.</li>
<li>A handle is present on the outside of the door to help with the maneuvering of the door.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="control-panel">Control Panel<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#control-panel" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>On the outer wall of the incubator is a control panel with all the switches and indicators that allows the parameters of the incubator to be controlled.</li>
<li>The control panel also has a switch to control the thermostat of the device.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thermostat">Thermostat<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thermostat" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A thermostat is used to set the desired temperature of the incubator.</li>
<li>After the desired temperature is reached, the thermostat automatically maintains the incubator at that temperature until the temperature is changed again.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="perforated-shelves">Perforated shelves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perforated-shelves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bound to the inner wall are some perforated shelves onto which the plates with the culture media are placed.</li>
<li>The perforations on the shelves allow the movement of hot air throughout the inside of the incubator.</li>
<li>In some incubators, the shelves are removable, which allows the shelves to be cleaned properly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="asbestos-door-gasket">Asbestos door gasket<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#asbestos-door-gasket" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The asbestos door gasket provides an almost airtight seal between the door and the cabinet.</li>
<li>This seal prevents the outside air from entering the cabinet and thus, creating an isolated hot environment inside the cabinet without being interrupted by the external environment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="l-shaped-thermometer">L-shaped thermometer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#l-shaped-thermometer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A thermometer is placed on the top part of the outer wall of the incubator.</li>
<li>One end of the thermometer provided with graduations remains outside of the incubator so that temperature can be read easily.</li>
<li>The next end with the mercury bulb is protruded slightly into the chamber of the incubator.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hepa-filters">HEPA filters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepa-filters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
84</p>
<ul>
<li>Some advanced incubators are also provided with HEPA filters to lower the possible contamination created due to airflow.</li>
<li>An air-pump with filters creates a closed-loop system so that the air flowing inside the incubator generates less contamination.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="humidity-and-gas-control">Humidity and gas control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#humidity-and-gas-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The CO₂ incubators are provided with a reservoir underneath the chamber that contains water.</li>
<li>The water is vaporized to maintain the relative humidity inside the chamber.</li>
<li>Similarly, these incubators are also provided with gas chambers to give the desired concentration of CO₂ inside the incubator.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principle-working-of-incubator">Principle/ Working of Incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principle-working-of-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>An incubator is based on the principle that microorganisms require a particular set of parameters for their growth and development.</li>
<li>All incubators are based on the concept that when organisms are provided with the optimal condition of temperature, humidity, oxygen, and carbon dioxide levels, they grow and divide to form more organisms.</li>
<li>In an incubator, the thermostat maintains a constant temperature that can be read from the outside via the thermometer.</li>
<li>The temperature is maintained by utilizing the heating and no-heating cycles.</li>
<li>During the heating cycle, the thermostat heats the incubator, and during the no-heating period, the heating is stopped, and the incubator is cooled by radiating heat to the surrounding.</li>
<li>Insulation from the outside creates an isolated condition inside the cabinet, which allows the microbes to grow effectively.</li>
<li>Similarly, other parameters like humidity and airflow are also maintained through different mechanisms that create an environment similar to the natural environment of the organisms.</li>
<li>Similarly, they are provided with adjustments for maintaining the concentration of CO₂ to balance the pH and humidity required for the growth of the organisms.</li>
<li>Variation of the incubator like a shaking incubator is also available, which allows for the continuous movement of the culture required for cell aeration and solubility studies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure-for-running-an-incubator">Procedure for running an incubator<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-for-running-an-incubator" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
85</p>
<p>Once the cultures of organisms are created, the culture plates are to be placed inside an incubator at the desired temperature and required period of time. In most clinical laboratories, the usual temperature to be maintained is 35–37°C for bacteria.</p>
<p>The following are the steps to be followed while running an incubator:</p>
<ol>
<li>Before using the incubator, it should be made sure that no remaining items are present in the incubator from the previous cycles. However, in some cases, if the same incubator is being used for multiple organisms, and they require the same set of parameters, they can be placed together in the same incubator.</li>
<li>The door of the incubator is then kept closed, and the incubator is switched on. The incubator has to be heated up to the desired temperature of the growth of the particular organism. The thermometer can be used to see if the temperature has reached.</li>
<li>In the meantime, if the organism requires a particular concentration of CO₂ or a specific humidity, those parameters should also be set in the incubator.</li>
<li>Once all the parameters are met, the petri dish cultures are placed on the perforated shelves upside down, i.e., media uppermost. This is necessary because if the plates are incubated normally, condensation collects on the surface of the medium and prevents the formation of isolated colonies.</li>
<li>If it is necessary to incubate Petri dish cultures for several days, the plates are sealed with adhesive tapes or are placed in plastic bags or plastic food containers.</li>
<li>Now, the door is locked, and the plates are kept inside for the required time before taking them out.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-incubators">Types of incubators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-incubators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On the basis of the presence of a particular parameter or the purpose of the incubator, incubators are divided into the following types:</p>
<p>a) Benchtop incubators</p>
<ul>
<li>This is the most common type of incubator used in most of the laboratories.</li>
<li>These incubators are the basic types of incubators with temperature control and insulation.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) CO2 incubators</p>
<ul>
<li>CO2 incubators are the special kinds of incubators that are provided with automatic control of CO2 and humidity.</li>
<li>This type of incubator is used for the growth of the cultivation of different bacteria requiring 5-10% of CO2 concentration.</li>
<li>For humidity control, water is kept underneath the cabinet of the incubator.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
86</p>
<p>c) Cooled incubators</p>
<ul>
<li>For incubation at temperatures below the ambient, incubators are fitted with modified refrigeration systems with heating and cooling controls.</li>
<li>This type of incubator is called the cooling incubator.</li>
<li>In the cooling incubator, the heating and cooling controls should be appropriately balanced.</li>
</ul>
<p>d) Shaker incubator</p>
<ul>
<li>A thermostatically controlled shaker incubator is another piece of apparatus used to cultivate microorganisms.</li>
<li>Its advantage is that it provides a rapid and uniform transfer of heat to the culture vessel, and its agitation provides increased aeration, resulting in acceleration of growth.</li>
<li>This incubator, however, can only be used for broth or liquid culture media.</li>
</ul>
<p>Portable incubator</p>
<ul>
<li>Portable incubators are smaller in size and are used in fieldwork, e.g. environmental microbiology and water examination.</li>
</ul>
<p>Uses of Incubator</p>
<p>Incubators have a wide range of applications in various areas including cell culture, pharmaceutical studies, hematological studies, and biochemical studies.</p>
<p>Some of the uses of incubators are given below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Incubators are used to grow microbial culture or cell cultures.</li>
<li>Incubators can also be used to maintain the culture of organisms to be used later.</li>
<li>Some incubators are used to increase the growth rate of organisms, having a prolonged growth rate in the natural environment.</li>
<li>Specific incubators are used for the reproduction of microbial colonies and subsequent determination of biochemical oxygen demand.</li>
<li>These are also used for breeding of insects and hatching of eggs in zoology.</li>
<li>Incubators also provide a controlled condition for sample storage before they can be processed in the laboratories.</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precautions">Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following precautions are to be followed while running an incubator:</p>
<ol>
<li>As microorganisms are susceptible to temperature change, the fluctuations in temperature of the cabinet by repeatedly opening the door should be avoided.</li>
<li>The required parameters growth of the organism should be met before the culture plates are placed inside the cabinet.</li>
<li>The plates should be placed upside down with the lid at the bottom to prevent the condensation of water on to the media.</li>
<li>The inside of the incubators should be cleaned regularly to prevent the organisms from settling on the shelves or the corners of the incubator.</li>
<li>While running the incubator for an extended period of time, sterile water should be placed underneath the shelves to prevent the culture media from drying out.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maintenance-of-bacterial-incubators">Maintenance of bacterial incubators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-bacterial-incubators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-clean-it-regularly">1. Clean It Regularly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-clean-it-regularly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If your incubator is contaminated, it's likely your results will be negatively impacted. As such, it's important to stick to a strict cleaning schedule for your unit. Some key steps to follow are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Always wear gloves when handling containers to be placed inside the unit.</li>
<li>If using a humidity pan, change the water in the pan at least once per week.</li>
<li>Clean the humidity pan, chamber, shelves, and any other removable parts regularly. Depending on the application, disinfection may be sufficient, or complete sterilization might be required. Make sure any disinfectants used won't harm your cell cultures or corrode the incubator chamber. <strong>Quaternary ammonium disinfectant</strong> is one of the best options for many applications.</li>
<li>Remember to clean the outside of the unit, especially the door handle.</li>
<li>Clean the fan and fan wheels every few months.</li>
<li>Some lab incubators include HEPA filters, which trap fine particulate matter present in the incoming air to reduce the potential for chamber contamination. Filters should be replaced every six months to one year.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-monitor-humidity-and-co2">2. Monitor Humidity and CO2<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-monitor-humidity-and-co2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Optimal growth conditions for cell cultures also include a specific humidity level and, in some cases, CO2 level. Tissues and cells are sensitive to changes in these parameters, so they need to be monitored closely.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
88</p>
<p>If the humidity is too low, there's a chance your cell culture media can evaporate or your growth media may become too concentrated. Ideal humidity is usually around 95%, and to keep it at this level, you need to make sure the water tray (under the incubator) is never at risk of running dry.</p>
<p>For CO2 incubators, you'll need to monitor the CO2 level. This is typically kept at 5% to maintain a constant pH for optimal growth. CO2 sensors help here by signaling when and how much CO2 needs to be added to the chamber. You can check CO2 levels using an external gas analyzer every few months.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-monitor-temperature">3. Monitor Temperature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-monitor-temperature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incubators are often maintained at 37°C for optimal growth of cell cultures. Deviations in temperature could inhibit growth or even destroy cultures. Temperature sensors are included units, but how do you know that you can always rely on your sensor? One way to ensure the correct temperature is use a second thermometer.</p>
<p>If your incubator has a glass door, you can attach a calibrated thermometer to the inside of the glass and read it without having to open the door. You can check this against the sensor temperature and if they're different, you know the sensor needs to be recalibrated.</p>
<p>Avoiding opening and closing the door unnecessarily can help keep the temperature stable (and prevent contaminants from entering the chamber). If you're concerned about the incubator door being inadvertently opened, you can opt for a unit with a door lock.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-place-your-unit-properly">4. Place Your Unit Properly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-place-your-unit-properly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Proper positioning of your unit can ensure it runs efficiently and has minimum exposure to potential contaminants. Here are the factors you need to consider when deciding on the perfect spot for your lab incubator:</p>
<ul>
<li>Doorways and vents can blow in contaminants and increase the chance of fungal growth. What's more, they can create drafts which can affect the temperature stability of your unit.</li>
<li>Direct sunlight can cause temperature fluctuations and issues with anti-condensation features.</li>
<li>You need enough space (at least three inches) around the unit so that heat can vent and cords and sockets are easily accessible.</li>
<li>Place floor incubators on a stand to limit the risk of contaminants sweeping in when the door is open.</li>
<li>Avoid humid, damp areas that may be harboring fungal growth.</li>
<li>Place units away from sources of vibration such as shakers, stirrers, or refrigerators, as vibrations can affect cell growth.</li>
<li>Ensure the area around the unit is as clean as possible.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
89</p>
<p>Ideal conditions for a lab incubator would be in a temperature-controlled environment and cleanroom conditions. As that is often not practical nor feasible, taking into account the factors above will suffice for most applications.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
90</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ph-meter">pH METER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ph-meter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The pH meter is a device used for determining the concentration of hydrogen ions [H+] in a solution. This equipment, provided it is carefully used and calibrated, measures the acidity of an aqueous solution. pH meters are sometimes called pH analyzers, pH monitors or potentiometers.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-fc3a00a5.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-b6f19ad9.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-8506131b.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<p>The pH meter is commonly used in any field of science related to aqueous solutions. It is used in areas such as agriculture, water treatment and purification, in industrial processes such as petrochemicals, paper manufacture, foods, pharmaceuticals, research and development, metal mechanics, etc.</p>
<p>In the health laboratory, its applications are related to the control of culture mediums and to the measurement of the alkalinity or acidity of broths and buffers.</p>
<p>In specialized laboratories, diagnostic equipment microelectrodes are used to measure the pH of liquid blood components. The plasma pH allows the patient's health to be evaluated. It normally measures between 7.35 and 7.45. This value relates to the patient's metabolism in which a multitude of reactions occurs where acids and bases are normally kept in balance.</p>
<p>Acids constantly liberate hydrogen ions [H+] and the organism neutralizes or balances acidity by liberating bicarbonate ions [HCO3-]. The acid-base ratio in the organism is maintained by the kidneys, (organs in which any excesses present are eliminated). The plasma pH is one of the characteristics that vary with factors such as age or state of health of the patient. The table below shows typical pH values of some bodily fluids;</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ph-meter-components">pH METER Components<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ph-meter-components" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A pH meter generally has the following components:</p>
<ol>
<li>The body of the instrument containing the circuits, controls, connectors, display screens and measuring scales. The following are among some of its most important components:</li>
</ol>
<p>a) An ON and OFF switch. Not all pH meters have an on and off switch. Some simply have a cord with a plug which allows it to be connected to a suitable electrical outlet.</p>
<p>b) Temperature control. This control allows adjustments according to the temperature of the solution measured.</p>
<p>c) Calibration controls. Depending on the design, pH meters possess one or two calibration buttons or dials. Normally these are identified by Cal 1 and Cal 2. If the pH meter is calibrated using only one solution, the Cal 1 button is used; making sure that Cal 2 is set at a 100%. If the pH meter allows two-point calibrations, two known pH solutions covering the range of pH to be measured are used. In this case, the two controls are used (Cal 1 and Cal 2). In special cases, a three-point calibration must be done (using three known pH solutions).</p>
<p>d) Mode selector. The functions generally included in this control are:</p>
<p>I. Standby mode (0). In this position the electrodes are protected from electrical currents. It is the position used for maintaining the equipment while stored.</p>
<p>II. pH mode. In this position the equipment can take pH measurements after performing the required calibration procedures.</p>
<p>III. Millivolt mode (mV). In this position the equipment is capable of performing millivoltage readings.</p>
<p>IV. ATC mode. The automatic temperature control mode is used when the pH is measured in</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
92</p>
<p>solutions for which the temperature varies. This function requires the use of a special probe. Not all pH meters have this control.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>A combined electrode or probe. This device must be stored in distilled water and stay connected to the measuring instrument. A combination electrode has a reference electrode (also known as Calomel electrode) and an internal electrode, integrated into the same body. Its design varies depending on the manufacturer.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="construction-of-ph-meter-combined-electrode">Construction of pH meter (combined electrode)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#construction-of-ph-meter-combined-electrode" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The pH probe of modern pH meter is a combined type, in which glass and reference electrode are placed into a rod like structure. The combined electrode consists of following parts-</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-a2049a4d.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg">
<a href="http://www.ph-meter.info/pH-electrode-single-double-junction" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.ph-meter.info/pH-electrode-single-double-junction</a></p>
<ol>
<li>Glass bulb: It is a sensor that senses the H+ ion concentration and it is made from special type of glass and membrane. The glass bulb consists of 0.1M HCL.</li>
<li>Internal electrode: It is the silver chloride electrode.</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
93</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Internal solution: The silver chloride electrode is dipped in buffer solution of 0.1 mol/L KCL of pH 7.</li>
<li>Reference Electrode: It is also the silver chloride electrode.</li>
<li>Internal Solution: The reference electrode is also dipped in buffer solution of 0.1 mol/L KCL of pH 7.</li>
<li>Junction: It is made from ceramic junction also called as diaphragm that allows the contact of sample solution and reference electrolyte. It does not disturb the electric connection between both the electrodes.</li>
<li>Filling hole: It is used for refilling the electrolyte.</li>
<li>Electrode body: the body is from non-conductive glass or plastic.</li>
</ol>
<p>The acidic solution is rich in H+ ion concentration. When pH probe is dipped in an acidic solution, the H+ ion moves close to the glass membrane of the sensitive glass bulb (external side of the bulb). Similar reaction occurs inside the bulb, which is filled with buffer solution of neutral pH. This neutral buffer solution has constant number of Hydrogen ions. The H+ ions present inside the bulb also moves close to glass membrane (internal side of the bulb). Hence, this causes the difference in the concentration of hydrogen ion or degree of hydrogen ion activity across the membrane causing difference in the potential (voltage). When the hydrogen ion concentration inside the glass bulb is less than the outside solution (test solution), then the given solution is acidic and hence the pH is lower than 7.</p>
<p>When the Hydrogen ions concentration across the membrane is same then it is called as neutral pH and the pH is equal to 7. If the concentration of hydrogen ion of inside the bulb than outside solution then the given solution is alkaline and the pH is more than 7. The pH meter measures the potential difference at both the electrodes and calculate the pH as per the Nernst equation.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
94</p>
