vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3603em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.04398em;">z</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">F</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">RT</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">ln</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>E</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> reduction potential</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>E</mi><mn>0</mn></msup><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">E^0 =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8141em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> standard potential</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>R</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> universal gas constant</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>T</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">T =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">T</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> temperature in kelvin</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>z</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">z =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.04398em;">z</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> ion charge (moles of electrons)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>F</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">F =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.13889em;">F</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> Faraday constant</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8778em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> reaction quotient</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principle-of-ph-meter">Principle of pH Meter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principle-of-ph-meter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>pH electrode is constructed of two half cells, which develop an electrical potential when connected together. Reference electrode maintains a constant potential and is bathed in KCl</p>
<p>Glass electrode (Sanz electrode) develops an electrical potential that is proportional to the amount of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi><mo>+</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{H}^+</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7713em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">H</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7713em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mbin mtight">+</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> present.</p>
<p>The working principle of the pH meter relies on the ions exchange from the sample solution to the inner solution (pH 7 buffer) of the glass electrode via the glass membrane. A pH meter has a pH probe to conduct the electrical signals to the pH meter, which then displays the pH value of the solution. The pH probe contains two electrodes, namely a sensor electrode and a reference electrode. One is filled with a pH 7 buffer, and the other with saturated potassium chloride solution. The sensor electrode bulb comprises a porous glass membrane coated with metal salts and silica.</p>
<p>When the probe is submerged in a sample solution to measure the pH, hydrogen ions build up around the bulb and take the place of the metal ions. Similarly, some metal ions transfer from the glass (sensor) electrode to the sample solution. Because of low sensitivity to pH changes or complete insensitivity to pH changes, the reference electrode potential offers a constant voltage. This generates some electricity captured by the silver wire by generating potential difference (hydrogen-ion activity). The pH meter converts the voltage of this electric flow into pH value by comparing the generated voltage to the reference electrode.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1</p>
<p>COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
95</p>
<p>Increasing the solution's acidity results in a higher concentration of hydrogen ions, which raises the voltage. The pH measurement on the pH meter decreases due to the increased voltage. Similar to how an increase in alkalinity reduces hydrogen ions, an increase in the concentration of hydroxyl ions also reduces the voltage and raises the pH reading on a pH meter.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-ed9184a7.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ph-meter-operating-procedure">pH Meter Operating Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ph-meter-operating-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Let all the samples get to the same temperature since pH readings rely on temperature. It is advised to compensate for temperature if the samples are not at 25 °C. Determine the temperatures of the samples using a thermometer and manually enter them into the meter, or use an ATC probe to communicate the temperatures automatically.</li>
<li>Uncover the sample beakers and prepare the samples.</li>
<li>Rinse the pH electrode in the sample beaker after rinsing it with deionized water beforehand. To prevent sample contamination, rinse the electrode with deionized water over a waste beaker. The identical beaker used for sample measurement should never be used to rinse the electrode.</li>
<li>The electrode should be inserted into the first sample measurement beaker with the electrode tip and junction completely submerged in the sample. The sample should then be stirred moderately and uniformly.</li>
<li>Set the meter to begin taking a reading.</li>
</ol>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
96</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>
<p>Record the pH and temperature of the sample after waiting at least 1 to 2 minutes for a stable reading in the sample.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If more samples are needed, repeat steps 3 through 6 again. For the most accurate sample measurements, submerge the electrode in each sample to the same depth. After measuring the samples, clean the electrode with deionized water and put it in a pH electrode storage solution.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-ph-meters">Types of pH meters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-ph-meters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-based-on-portability">A. Based on Portability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-based-on-portability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Pen testers: Pen testers are portable, inexpensive pH meters the size of a pocketbook. The compact form makes them incredibly simple to transport and use while on the road. They are designed with a pH meter, display, and electrode. Pen testers have many uses in the building, hydroponics, food production, and pool or spa care industries.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Handheld meters: Handheld meters often have a more robust build and a slightly larger shape than pen testers. With this design, the electrode is constructed independently of the meter. Depending on your demands for pH measurement, handheld meters typically feature electrodes you may switch out. For medium-to-firm items, for instance, spear-tipped electrodes are utilized. Hand-held meters are designed for usage in the field. Environmental officers use them in field research, aquaculture, agriculture, and water treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Benchtop pH meters: The largest of the three pH meter categories are benchtop meters. They can be put on a wall or a desk. They are often the most accurate pH meters available, which makes them ideal for usage in laboratories and professional settings. Benchtop pH meters are frequently used in laboratories for environmental monitoring, water testing facilities, and food processing facilities.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-based-on-usage">B. Based on Usage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-based-on-usage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Laboratory pH meter: It has a large measuring range, is highly accurate, and is versatile.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Industrial pH meter: Its distinctive qualities, which combine analog output, digital intelligence, and upper and lower boundary alarm and control functions, include</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1

97</p>
<p>exceptional stability, steady work, a high level of measurement efficiency, environmental flexibility, and anti-interference capabilities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-based-on-reading">C. Based on reading<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-based-on-reading" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Analog pH meter: An analog pH meter is the original type of model. A pointer will show the pH level on analog pH meters. The needle will move toward a number representing the pH level after the measuring electrode has been put into the sample. When using an analog pH meter, one must be careful to obtain accurate findings. The little pointer is the reason for this.</li>
<li>Digital pH meter: The development of analog pH meters led to the creation of the digital pH meter. The number printed on a digital pH meter’s measuring device is a clue as to what pH level is being measured. This makes it simpler to obtain accurate results concerning samples. However, the basic operations of analog and digital pH meters are still the same.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="applications-of-ph-meter">Applications of pH meter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#applications-of-ph-meter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>A pH meter is essential for assessing soil in the agricultural sector. A pH meter is required because major crops need an alkaline climate. Additionally, they are utilized to gauge the pH of the soil, which will aid in maximizing returns and yields from the soil.</li>
<li>Monitoring pH level is essential in water treatment facilities and RO water purifiers.</li>
<li>Chemical industries use pH meters to neutralize wastewater from the steel, pulp, paper, pharmaceutical, biotech, and petrochemical industries.</li>
<li>A pH meter determines the pH value of chemical compounds and food products to ensure their quality and safety.</li>
<li>The food industry specifically uses pH meters in the context of dairy products.</li>
<li>To determine the type of biological conditions by measuring the pH of biological fluids such as blood, urine, gastric acid, etc.</li>
<li>Employed in detergent manufacturing.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-ph-meters">Advantages of pH Meters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-ph-meters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
98</p>
<ol>
<li>Well-matched for continuous automatic recording and control of industrial and commercial processes</li>
<li>Permits rapid and reproducible measurements</li>
<li>Simple to control and operate.</li>
<li>Used for both oxidizing and reducing solutions</li>
<li>Does not affect the solution under examination.</li>
<li>Suitable for use in colloidal, turbid, and colorful solutions.</li>
<li>This device gives the most accurate and precise value of pH.</li>
<li>pH meters are portable, so they can be easily used everywhere while traveling.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="limitations-of-ph-meter">Limitations of pH meter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limitations-of-ph-meter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>pH meters should be regularly cleaned to avoid possible contamination of samples. When exposed to corrosive chemicals, the glass tip of the probe used in pH meters can easily break or get damaged.</li>
<li>External factors like temperature impact the output readings of the pH meter. Thus, pH meters must be calibrated before use to obtain accurate results unless our results may be distorted.</li>
<li>Deposits on electrode membranes can affect the processes.</li>
<li>A special buffer solution is needed to calibrate the pH meters.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precautions">Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>pH electrodes are sensitive and fragile, so one should not use them as a glass rod to stir the solution while measuring pH.</li>
<li>pH meters should be calibrated daily before use with the help of standard buffer solutions.</li>
<li>pH readings are temperature sensitive, so pH meters shouldn't be exposed to sunlight.</li>
<li>All the test tubes and glass apparatus used in measurement should be cleaned with distilled water before use.</li>
<li>For each new sample, either uses a brand-new fine dropper or glass rod or thoroughly wash the dropper or rod in water between uses.</li>
<li>All the solutions used in measurement should be freshly prepared.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="water-bath">WATER BATH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A water bath is a scientific equipment used to maintain a steady temperature for a prolonged time when incubating samples.</p>
<p>A big container filled with warm water makes up a hot water bath. It has different design combinations, sizes, and proportions. A laboratory water bath’s container capacity ranges from 12 to 32 liters for a standard model and 50 to 100 liters for a large water bath. Most water baths feature a digital or analog interface that users may use to set the desired temperature.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-3b5837e2.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<p>Its mostly utilized in clinical and microbiology labs, university labs, environmental research, and even food technology for warming reagents, sample thawing, corrosion tests, and bacteriological investigations, among other applications. A water bath is a tool that needs additional supporting instruments to function. An incubator, a micropipette, a centrifuge, and a laboratory oven are typically used in tests involving a water bath.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="operation-principles">Operation Principles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operation-principles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Water baths are made of steel and are generally covered with electrostatic paint with high adherence and resistance to environmental laboratory conditions. Water baths have an external panel on which the controls can be found. They also have a tank made of rustproof material with a collection of electrical resistors mounted on their lower part. By means of these, heat is transferred to the medium (water or oil) until reaching the temperature selected with a control device (thermostat or similar). The resistors may be of the following types:</p>
<ul>
<li>Immersion type. These resistors are installed inside a sealed tube and located on the lower part of the container in direct contact with heating medium.</li>
<li>External. These resistors are located on the lower part but on the outside of the tank. These are protected by an isolating material which prevents heat loss. This type of resistor transfers the heat to the bottom of the tank through thermal conduction.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="parts-of-a-water-bath">Parts of a Water Bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parts-of-a-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tank</li>
</ul>
<p>A laboratory water bath’s container comprises an insulated metal, like stainless steel. Test samples are maintained in hot water for a lengthy time in a container.</p>
<ul>
<li>Container lid</li>
</ul>

<p>It is mainly constructed of insulated metal or heat-resistant glass. The lid keeps the container covered, preventing water evaporation.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Heating elements
Source of heat in a laboratory water bath to help create heat.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thermometer
It helps gauge the water bath’s temperature. It may be integrated or added on its own.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thermostat or regulator
It aids in maintaining a steady temperature in a water bath.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Propeller or stirrer device
It is found in circulating water baths which promotes water circulation inside it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Outlet
It aids in removing the water from the container.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indicator light
It should be present in every water bath. It lights on when the water bath is warming. The light will be turned off to maintain the desired temperature if the water bath achieves it.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Types of Water bath</p>
<ol>
<li>Shaking Water Bath
The water bath’s shaking characteristic is more precisely controlled for liquid flow. An on/off switch controls the shaking. In microbiological techniques, regular shaking allows liquid-grown cell cultures to mix continuously with the air. The features of the shaking water bath include high-precision temperature control, easy temperature adjustment, a precise and clear indication, and outstanding and dependable performance. For easier experimental observation, lighting equipment is provided in the workshop. The cabinet has a fan, and a forced-air convection unit fitted to disperse heat more evenly.</li>
</ol>
<p>Some of the main benefits of this type of water bath include the user-friendly keypad operation, the straightforward bath drains, the programmable shaking frequencies, etc.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Circulating Water Bath
It is also known as a stirrer water bath. In the baths with circulating water, the water is properly circulating. Stirrers or circulating water baths may be useful for applications where the samples must have consistent or uniform temperatures. The circulating water bath uses continuously circulating water to efficiently and dependably obtain and maintain the desired water temperatures required for the cooling or heating of samples and reagents. It enables quick heating or cooling of samples across a wide temperature range. Enzymatic and serologic testing may be used for these purposes. It receives proper circulation, which leads to a more stable temperature.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non-circulating Water Bath
Such laboratory water baths rely on the convection mechanism rather than heating the water uniformly. As a result, the water bath’s capacity to control temperature is less exact. We can also add accessories to stir the water bath to enhance heat transmission. Water baths are safe to use up to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>99.9</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">99.9^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">99.</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">9</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>. When the temperature is greater than <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>100</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">100^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>, substitutes may be used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Polycarbonate Water Bath</p>
</li>
</ol>

<p>Inside the bath, there is a controlled heating system. The container/tank is made of transparent polycarbonate, and its temperature can reach 100 degrees Fahrenheit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="analogue-and-digital-water-baths">Analogue and Digital Water Baths<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analogue-and-digital-water-baths" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="analog-water-bath">Analog water bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analog-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The most basic kind of water bath is an analog one. It is affordable and simple to use. However, it only has a few issues. The analog water bath’s accuracy is lower than the digital water bath’s, which is the first issue. There isn’t a display board in addition to that. The water’s true temperature won’t be visible as a result.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="working-mechanism-of-analog-water-bath">Working mechanism of analog water bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#working-mechanism-of-analog-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>When the machine is given a power supply, the main indicator will glow. Then the current will go to the thermostat. From the thermostat, the current will flow through the water immersion heater. The thermostat will permit current to pass through the heating rod if the water’s temperature is lower than the predetermined level. Consequently, the water will start to warm up. The thermostat will shut off when the water temperature reaches the predetermined level. The heating rod won’t, therefore, receive any current. The water’s temperature then starts to drop. The heating indicator will also stop glowing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="digital-water-bath">Digital water bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#digital-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>An upgraded version of an analog water bath is a digital water bath. It’s extremely pricey. However, using it is simple. This version is more accurate. Similar to that, it has a display board that enables the user to view the real temperature of the bath’s water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="working-mechanism-of-digital-water-bath">Working Mechanism of digital water bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#working-mechanism-of-digital-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The solid-state relay (SSR) and PID controller work together to manage the water immersion heater. The controller will deliver a certain DC voltage to the relay if the water temperature is below the predetermined value. The relay will turn on, causing the AC to flow to the heating rod. As a result, the heater starts to warm the water. The PID controller will constantly activate and deactivate the relay when the actual temperature of the water approaches the desired value. Thus, the heating rod will continuously cycle ON and OFF. As a result, the water bath contributes to the maintenance of a nearly precise result with a variance of no more than <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>1</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1^{\circ}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>. The sensor measures the water’s temperature using a resistance temperature detector (RTD). The temperature is then converted to a resistance value, which is supplied to the controller. This incoming signal will be compared to the preset value by the controller.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="controls-of-a-laboratory-water-bath">Controls of a Laboratory Water Bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#controls-of-a-laboratory-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Temperature controller</strong>: A temperature controller, either digital or dial, is a standard feature of all water baths.</p>
<p><strong>Safety controller</strong>: A safety controller is often found above the temperature controller or connected to the indicator light in most water baths. A safety controller aids in determining the highest temperature that the water bath should reach. The safety light will turn on if the water bath somehow manages to meet the temperature that the safety controller has established. Even with a higher temperature, a water bath cannot achieve a temperature greater than the safety settings.</p>
<p><strong>Shaking controller</strong>: It may enable us to accelerate, decelerate, or activate the shaker.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="operating-procedure-of-water-bath">Operating procedure of Water Bath<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#operating-procedure-of-water-bath" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<ol>
<li>Ensure the equipment is clean and the temperature indicator is calibrated by the due date.</li>
<li>Plug in the power source.</li>
<li>Make sure the water in the bath has enough depth for the heating element to be poured in.</li>
<li>Turn “ON” the instrument’s main power source.</li>
<li>In order to set the desired temperature, press the SET key. The temperature can be changed by pressing any or both of these buttons.</li>
<li>Use a calibrated thermometer to confirm the temperature.</li>
<li>The temperature sensor will retain the set temperature whenever a water bath is used.</li>
<li>After use, turn “OFF” the main power source and the instrument’s mains.</li>
<li>After usage, completely dry the instrument and then replace the lid.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="applications">Applications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#applications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It can be used for reagent warming, substrate melting, or cell culture incubation.</li>
<li>The water bath is the preferred heat source for heating flammable compounds because it allows some chemical processes to occur at high temperatures.</li>
<li>It improves the solubility of poorly soluble compounds.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Samples can be heated evenly in the lab water bath, avoiding direct heating’s excessive intensity and uncontrollable temperature swings.</li>
<li>Water baths offer a larger surface area, allowing your samples to be heated more quickly.</li>
<li>Even if you are simultaneously heating several samples, there is very little chance of temperature variations because water baths can hold a significant amount of heat.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="limitations">Limitations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limitations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Like an untreated hot tub, warm water exposed to the environment can hold and support undesirable microbial activity.</li>
<li>If tap water is used in the water bath, it must be replaced frequently; distilled water does not require frequent replacement.</li>
<li>It is solely reliant on power and is not suitable for the usage of heat-sensitive samples.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precautions">Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Make sure the bath is seemingly electrically safe before its use. For instance, a current safety check could be performed for obvious issues with the main connector and lead, external switches, or controls.</li>
<li>Before turning on/operating controls and plugging into a mains power outlet, make sure your hands are dry.</li>
<li>Avoid touching the shaker mechanism or circulation impeller with your hands, hair, or loose clothing. If possible and appropriate, cover your device when operating at temperatures exceeding “hand hot” (&gt;50°C).</li>
<li>Make that the water level is kept at the proper level, especially when operating at higher temperatures, such as those close to 95°C. Water levels should be routinely checked, and only distilled water should be used to fill them. This is necessary to stop salts from building up on the heater. Do not rely on the thermal cut-out functioning well when the heating elements are not covered by water; this will prevent overheating and potential electrical damage.</li>
<li>Use an appropriate algicide, fungicide, or bactericide if the bath will be used constantly for a long time, such as &gt;24 hours, to prevent the growth of undesired and potentially</li>
</ul>

<p>pathogenic organisms in the bath water. To reduce hazards from corrosion, leaks, and electrical failures, this must be compatible with the tank's materials and other parts.</p>
<ul>
<li>Ensure to thoroughly clean the bath after usage, especially if it was used to incubate potentially pathogenic sources and poisonous or caustic items that could end up in the bath water. If powerful detergents or disinfectants are to be used, wear rubber gloves and perhaps eye protection.</li>
<li>Avoid using the water bath with the substances indicated below:
a) Bleach.
b) Liquids with high chlorine content.
c) Weak saline solutions such as sodium chloride, calcium chloride or chromium compounds.
d) Strong concentrations of any acid.
e) Strong concentrations of any salt.
f) Weak concentrations of hydrochloric, hydrobromic, hydroiodic, sulphuric or chromic acids.
g) Deionized water, as it causes corrosion and perforation in the stainless steel.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintenance">Maintenance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Warning: Before carrying out any maintenance activity, disconnect the equipment from the electrical feed outlet.</p>
<p>Water baths are equipment whose maintenance is simple. The recommended routines mainly focus on the cleaning of external components. The most common routines are featured next.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning">Cleaning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="frequency-monthly">Frequency: Monthly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-monthly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Turn off and disconnect the equipment. Wait until it cools to avoid the risk of burns and accidents.</li>
<li>Remove the fluid used for heating. If it is water, it can be poured through a siphon. If it is oil; collect into a container with an adequate capacity.</li>
<li>Remove the thermal diffusion grid located at the bottom of the tank.</li>
<li>Disassemble the circulator and clean to remove scale and potential algae present.</li>
<li>Clean the interior of the tank with a mild detergent. If there is any indication of corrosion, use substances for cleaning stainless steel. Rub lightly with synthetic sponges or equivalent. Avoid using steel wool to remove rust stains as these leave particles of steel which could accelerate corrosion.</li>
<li>Avoid bending or striking the temperature control capillary tube generally located at the bottom of the tank.</li>
<li>Clean the exterior and interior of the water bath with clean water.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lubrication">Lubrication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lubrication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="frequency-daily">Frequency: Daily<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-daily" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>For water baths with an agitation unit or circulator system: Lubricate the axis of the circulator's electric motor. Put a drop of mineral oil on the axis so that a good lubricating condition is maintained between the motor's bearings and its axis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="periodic-inspection">Periodic inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#periodic-inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="frequency-quarterly">Frequency: Quarterly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-quarterly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Check the thermometer or temperature controls every three months using known standards. If no reference standard is available, use an ice/water mixture and/or boiling water.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pulse-oximeters">PULSE OXIMETERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pulse-oximeters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pulse oximetry is a rapid, noninvasive method of estimating oxygenation and is continuous, allowing detection of sudden changes in a patient’s clinical status.</p>
<p>A pulse oximeter, utilized in pulse oximetry, is a device that non-invasively monitors the oxygen saturation of a patient's blood. The colored substance in blood, hemoglobin, is carrier of oxygen and the absorption of light by hemoglobin varies with the amount of oxygenation. Two different kinds of light (one visible, one invisible) are directed through the skin from one side of a probe, and the amount transmitted is measured on the other side.</p>
<p>The machine converts the ratio of transmission of the two kinds of light into a % oxygenation. Pulse oximeter probes can be mounted on the finger or ear lobe.</p>
<p>There are TWO numerical values obtained from the pulse oximeter monitor:</p>
<ul>
<li>The oxygen saturation of haemoglobin in arterial blood. The value of the oxygen saturation is given together with an audible signal that varies in pitch depending on the oxygen saturation. A falling pitch indicates falling oxygen saturation. Since the oximeter detects the saturation peripherally on a finger, toe or ear, the result is recorded as the peripheral oxygen saturation, described as SpO2.</li>
<li>The pulse rate in beats per minute, averaged over 5 to 20 seconds. Some oximeters display a pulse waveform or indicator that illustrates the strength of the pulse being detected. This display indicates how well the tissues are perfused. The signal strength falls if the circulation becomes inadequate.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oxygen-saturation">Oxygen saturation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oxygen-saturation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Red blood cells contain haemoglobin. One molecule of haemoglobin can carry up to four molecules of oxygen after which it is described as “saturated” with oxygen. If all the binding sites on the haemoglobin molecule are carrying oxygen, the haemoglobin is said to have a saturation of 100%. Most of the haemoglobin in blood combines with oxygen as it passes through the lungs. A healthy individual with normal lungs, breathing air at sea level, will have an arterial oxygen saturation of 95% – 100%. Extremes of altitude will affect these numbers. Venous blood that is collected from the tissues contains less oxygen and normally has a</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
107</p>
<p>saturation of around 75%. Arterial blood looks bright red whilst venous blood looks dark red. The difference in colour is due to the difference in haemoglobin saturation. When patients are well saturated, their tongues and lips appear pink in colour; when they are desaturated, they appear blue. This is called cyanosis. It can be difficult to see cyanosis clinically, particularly in a dark-skinned patient. You may not notice this sign until the oxygen saturation is less than 90%. Detecting cyanosis is even more difficult in a poorly lit operating theatre. Cyanosis is only visible when the deoxygenated haemoglobin concentration is greater than 5 g/dl. A severely anaemic patient may not appear cyanosed even when extremely hypoxic as there is very little haemoglobin circulating through the tissues. If the oxygen saturation is 94% or lower, the patient is hypoxic and needs to be treated quickly. A saturation of less than 90% is a clinical emergency.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-758390ea.jpeg" alt="img-44.jpeg">
Figure 18: Pulse Oximeter</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-c912ee0c.jpeg" alt="img-45.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-a-pulse-oximeter">Components of a pulse oximeter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-a-pulse-oximeter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A pulse oximeter consists of the monitor containing the batteries and display, and the probe that senses the pulse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-pulse-oximeter-monitor">The Pulse Oximeter Monitor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-pulse-oximeter-monitor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The monitor contains the microprocessor and display. The display shows the oxygen saturation, the pulse rate and the waveform detected by the sensor. The monitor is connected to the patient via the probe. During use, the monitor updates its calculations regularly to give an immediate reading of oxygen saturation and pulse rate. The pulse indicator is continuously displayed to give information about the 10 circulations. The audible beep changes pitch with the value of oxygen saturation and is an important safety feature. The pitch drops as the saturation falls and rises as it</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
108</p>
<p>recovers. This allows for easier hearing of changes in the oxygen saturation immediately, without having to look at the monitor all the time. The monitor is delicate. It is sensitive to rough handling and excessive heat and can be damaged by spilling fluids on it. The monitor can be cleaned by gently wiping with a damp cloth. When not in use, it should be connected to an electrical supply to ensure that the battery is fully charged.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-pulse-oximeter-probe">The Pulse Oximeter probe<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-pulse-oximeter-probe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The oximeter probe consists of two parts; the <strong>light emitting diodes</strong> (LEDs) and a <strong>light detector</strong> (called a photo-detector). Beams of light are shone through the tissues from one side of the probe to the other. The blood and tissues absorb some of the light emitted by the probe. The light absorbed by the blood varies with the oxygen saturation of haemoglobin. The photo-detector detects the light transmitted as the blood pulses through the tissues and the microprocessor calculates a value for the oxygen saturation (SpO2). In order for the pulse oximeter to function, the probe must be placed where a pulse can be detected. The LEDs must face the light detector in order to detect the light as it passes through the tissues. The probe emits a red light when the machine is switched on; check that you can see this light to make sure the probe is working properly. Probes are designed for use on the finger, toe or ear lobe. They are of different types. <strong>Hinged probes</strong> are the most popular, but are easily damaged. <strong>Rubber probes</strong> are the most robust. The wrap around design may constrict the blood flow through the finger if put on too tightly. <strong>Ear probes</strong> are lightweight and are useful in children or if the patient is very vasoconstricted. Small probes have been designed for children but an adult hinged probe may be used on the thumb or big toe of a child. For finger or toe probes, the manufacturer marks the correct orientation of the nail bed on the probe.</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
109</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251216-f9df7c27.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg">
Hinged finger probe showing connector that can only be connected to the oximeter one way by aligning the gap on the probe connector with the corresponding notch on the machine.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="practical-use-of-the-pulse-oximeter">Practical use of the pulse oximeter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#practical-use-of-the-pulse-oximeter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Turn the pulse oximeter on: it will go through internal calibration and checks.</li>
<li>Select the appropriate probe with particular attention to correct sizing and where it will go (usually finger, toe or ear). If used on a finger or toe, make sure the area is clean. Remove any nail varnish.</li>
<li>Connect the probe to the pulse oximeter.</li>
<li>Position the probe carefully; make sure it fits easily without being too loose or too tight.</li>
<li>If possible, avoid the arm being used for blood pressure monitoring as cuff inflation will interrupt the pulse oximeter signal.</li>
<li>Allow several seconds for the pulse oximeter to detect the pulse and calculate the oxygen saturation.</li>
<li>Look for the displayed pulse indicator that shows that the machine has detected a pulse. Without a pulse signal, any readings are meaningless.</li>
<li>Once the unit has detected a good pulse, the oxygen saturation and pulse rate will be displayed.</li>
<li>Like all machines, oximeters may occasionally give a false reading - if in doubt, rely on your clinical judgement, rather than the machine.</li>
<li>The function of the oximeter probe can be checked by placing it on your own finger.</li>
<li>Adjust the volume of the audible pulse beep to a comfortable level for your theatre – never use on silent.</li>
<li>Always make sure the alarms are on.</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
110</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pulse-oximeter-alarms">Pulse Oximeter Alarms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pulse-oximeter-alarms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Alarms alert the anaesthetist to clinical problems. The alarms are as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Low saturation emergency (hypoxia) i.e. SpO2 &lt;90%, The oxygen saturation in healthy patients of any age should be 95% or above.</li>
<li>No pulse detected: alarm is commonly caused by the probe coming off the finger, but it may also be triggered if the patient is hypotensive, hypovolaemic, or has suffered a cardiac arrest. Check the probe site quickly and then assess the patient</li>
<li>Low pulse rate;</li>
<li>High pulse rate</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-interfering-with-the-pulse-oximeter-readings">Factors interfering with the pulse oximeter readings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-interfering-with-the-pulse-oximeter-readings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Several factors can interfere with the correct function of a pulse oximeter including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Light – bright light (such as the operating theatre light or sunlight) directly on the probe may affect the reading. Shield the probe from direct light.</li>
<li>Shivering – movement may make it difficult for the probe to pick up a signal.</li>
<li>Pulse volume – the oximeter only detects pulsatile flow. When the blood pressure is low due to hypovolaemic shock or the cardiac output is low or the patient has an arrhythmia, the pulse may be very weak and the oximeter may not be able to detect a signal</li>
<li>Vasoconstriction reduces blood flow to the peripheries. The oximeter may fail to detect a signal if the patient is very cold and peripherally vasoconstricted.</li>
<li>Carbon monoxide poisoning may give a falsely high saturation reading. Carbon monoxide binds very well to haemoglobin and displaces oxygen to form a bright red compound called carboxyhemoglobin. This is only an issue in patients following smoke inhalation from a fire.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="application-of-pulse-oximeters">Application of pulse oximeters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#application-of-pulse-oximeters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Doctors use pulse oximetry for a number of different reasons, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>to assess how well a new lung medication is working</li>
<li>to evaluate whether someone needs help breathing</li>
<li>to evaluate how helpful a ventilator is</li>
<li>to monitor oxygen levels during or after surgical procedures that require sedation</li>
<li>to determine whether someone needs supplemental oxygen therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING | TEACHING NOTES – VOLUME 1
COMPILED BY A. O. ONYANGO
This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>CLINICAL ENGINEERING I
111</p>
<ul>
<li>to determine how effective supplemental oxygen therapy is, especially when treatment is new</li>
<li>to assess someone’s ability to tolerate increased physical activity</li>
<li>to evaluate whether someone momentarily stops breathing while sleeping — like in cases of sleep apnea — during a sleep study</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maintenance-of-pulse-oximeters">Maintenance of pulse oximeters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintenance-of-pulse-oximeters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The oximeter probe is the most delicate part of a pulse oximeter and is easily damaged. Handle the probe carefully and never leave it in a place where it could be dropped on the floor.</p>
<p>The probe connects to the oximeter using a connector with a series of very fine pins that can be easily damaged. Always align the connector correctly before attempting to insert it into the monitor.</p>
<p>Never pull the probe from the machine by pulling on the cable; always grasp the connector firmly between finger and thumb</p>
<p>When not in use, the oximeter probe cable may be loosely coiled for storage or carrying, but should not be coiled too tightly as this will damage the wires inside the cable.</p>
<p>The lens and detector should be kept clean. Use soapy water or an alcohol-soaked swab to gently clean dust, dirt or blood from the probe.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2d52b8b8">Troubleshooting – Pulse Oximeters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2d52b8b8" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Fault</th><th>Possible Cause</th><th>Solution</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1. Equipment is not running</td><td>No power from mains socket</td><td>Check power switch is on.</td></tr><tr><td>Replace fuse with correct voltage and current if blown.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Check mains power is present at socket using equipment known to be working. Contact electrician for rewiring if power not present.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Battery (if present) is discharged</td><td>Recharge or replace battery</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Electrical cable fault</td><td>Try cable on another piece of equipment. Contact electrician for repair if required.</td></tr><tr><td>2. SpO_{2} or pulse rate not displayed or unstable</td><td>Probe is not mounted correctly</td><td>Connect probe and cable properly</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Probe not able to read through dirt, nail polish, etc.</td><td>Remove grease, dirt, nail polish and clean probe</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Patient movement</td><td>Request patient to remain still</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Patient’s SpO_{2} value is too low to be measured</td><td>Further clinical examination of patient. Resite probe if necessary</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Internal malfunction</td><td>Call biomedical technician.</td></tr><tr><td>3. “Probe off” displayed on screen</td><td>Probe is not connected properly</td><td>Connect the sensor</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>The connection between the probe and oximeter is loose</td><td>Refer to biomedical technician for repair</td></tr><tr><td>4. “Error” displayed on screen</td><td>Faulty probe or control circuit</td><td>Refer to biomedical technician</td></tr><tr><td>5. Continuous alarm sounds</td><td>Alarm limits set too low or high</td><td>Set appropriate alarm limits</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Power disconnected</td><td>Connect power cable</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Internal malfunction</td><td>Refer to biomedical technician</td></tr><tr><td>6. Electrical shocks</td><td>Wiring fault</td><td>Refer to biomedical technician immediately</td></tr></tbody></table>

<p>User Maintenance Checklist – Pulse Oximeters</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Daily</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Cleaning</td><td>✓ Remove any dust / dirt and replace equipment cover</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>✓ Remove any tape, paper or foreign body from equipment</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>✓ Clean probe with alcohol wipe after each use</td></tr><tr><td>Visual checks</td><td>✓ Check all parts are present and connected</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>✓ Check cables are not twisted and remove from service if any damage is visible</td></tr><tr><td>Function checks</td><td>✓ Check operation on healthy subject before use</td></tr><tr><td>Weekly</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td></tr><tr><td>Cleaning</td><td>✓ Unplug, clean outside with damp cloth and dry off</td></tr><tr><td>Visual checks</td><td>✓ Tighten any loose screws and check parts are fitted tightly</td></tr><tr><td>✓ If plug, cable or socket are damaged, replace</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Function checks</td><td>✓ Check operation of all lights, indicators and visual displays</td></tr><tr><td>✓ Check probe disconnection alarm.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Every six months</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Biomedical Technician check required</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
